## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of time t and current concentration A, which is the fundamental problem of determining rate laws in chemical kinetics. The rate law may involve integer or fractional reaction orders, reversible reactions, or complex mechanisms where other species concentrations have been eliminated.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with equilibrium)
- Reversible second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate expression from reversible mechanism)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed reaction with stoichiometric constraint)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics / saturation kinetics)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (enzyme kinetics with inhibition)
- Time-dependent effective rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate with time-dependent pseudo-species)
- Coupled elimination rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - c2 * A) (second species eliminated via stoichiometry)
- Mixed order with time: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (empirical power-law in both A and t)
- Consecutive reaction effective: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * A (effective rate from coupled ODEs)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Stoichiometric constraints appear as polynomial terms like A*(c-A), reflecting conservation of total concentration among coupled species
- Integer reaction orders (1, 2, 3) are strongly preferred in elementary reactions; fractional orders suggest complex mechanisms
- Negative rate constants indicate consumption of the species (reactant), positive indicate production (product formation)
- When other species are eliminated via stoichiometry (e.g., B = B0 - A), the rate law becomes a polynomial in A with coefficients encoding initial conditions
- Explicit time dependence in dA/dt often arises from integrating out intermediate species in consecutive reaction mechanisms (A→B→C)
- Saturation-type denominators (Michaelis-Menten) arise from quasi-steady-state approximation of enzyme-substrate complexes
- Cubic or higher polynomial terms in A suggest trimolecular steps or multiple coupled equilibria
- Oscillatory kinetics (e.g., Belousov-Zhabotinsky) produce cross-terms and cubic nonlinearities in concentration
- Equilibrium constants appear as ratios of forward/reverse rate constants, manifesting as additive constant terms in the rate expression
